         <img alt="large_2014_MeschFinal_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_MeschFinal_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         L is for lobster.
        </h3>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_LobbyExtra_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_LobbyExtra_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_05.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_05.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         It wouldn't be summer in the Hamptons without lobster, and one of the best ways to enjoy it is stuffed into one of the insanely huge lobster rolls at Canal Cafe in Hampton Bays.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_AGNap_3.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_AGNap_3.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_10.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_10.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_09.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_09.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Served not on a measly hot-dog bun like a traditional lobster roll, but on a hearty, nearly foot-long baguette, Canal Cafe's lobster roll is positively bursting with fresh lobster meat and not much else.  I hold these lobster rolls personally responsible for the state of Angel's waistline from April through October.
        </p>
        <p>
         If lobster rolls aren't your thing, head on over to the Lobster Inn, a classic seafood shack where the namesake dish can be grilled, steamed, stuffed, or served as a "splat," which comes with steamers, hard clams, mussels, shrimp, and crab.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_02.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_02.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_03.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_03.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_07.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_07.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Lobsters_08.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Lobsters_08.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         M is for money to burn.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Everywhere
         <em>
          else
         </em>
         in the world, that's a metaphor.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Moneytoburn_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Moneytoburn_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         N is for neighbors.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Our neighbors Norma and Daniel are two of the kindest, most generous people we've ever had the pleasure of knowing.  Norma brings us things like homemade garlic-herb bread made with fresh rosemary from her garden and homemade caponata with her garden basil, while Daniel brings us goodies like homemade cherry-basil vodka and invites us over to "the Bungalow," as he charmingly calls it, for BBQ chicken and coconut cupcakes.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Friends_12.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Friends_12.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Friends_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Friends_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Friends_14.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Friends_14.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Friends_15.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Friends_15.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         All of which is to say, these two could be complete jerks and we'd still keep 'em around.
        </p>
        <h3>
         O is for our wedding.
        </h3>
        <p>
         On August 5, 2000, Angel and I exchanged our wedding vows at the Westhampton Bath &amp; Tennis Club on Dune Road.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wedding_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wedding_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wedding_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wedding_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_WeddingCenter_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_WeddingCenter_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wedding_8.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wedding_8.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         There were some bumps along the way -- the cake was inexplicably the wrong color, and the lobsters weren't de-shelled even though we'd paid extra to make sure they would be -- but we were surrounded by the people we love the most . . . in the place we love the most.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wedding_4.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wedding_4.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wedding_7.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wedding_7.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         And
         <em>
          that
         </em>
         made it perfect.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wedding_5.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wedding_5.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         P is for Plaza Cafe.
        </h3>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_PlazaCafe_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_PlazaCafe_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         I have three words for you: Lobster. Shepherd's. Pie.  What's better than three words, or even 1,000?  You know.
         <br/>
         <br/>
         <img alt="large_2014_PlazaCafe_05.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_PlazaCafe_05.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_PlazaCafe_08.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_PlazaCafe_08.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         That feat of seafoody splendor is served up by Bari, one of the sweetest and most knowledgeable waitresses around, and cooked up by chef Doug Gulija, one of those maddening people who is insanely talented but also extremely nice.  This guy could be cooking up frozen fish sticks and I guarantee they'd be the best you'd ever had.   Luckily, though, there's stuff like pumpkin-lobster bisque; shrimp with porcini risotto; soy and acacia honey marinated black cod with yuzu beurre blanc; and red snapper stuffed with lobster instead.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_PlazaCafe_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_PlazaCafe_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_PlazaCafe_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_PlazaCafe_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_PlazaCafe_07.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_PlazaCafe_07.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         Q is for Quogue.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Our friends Jennifer and James joined us for a weekend in the Hamptons last summer, and we took them to lunch at Dockers in East Quogue, a gorgeous little oceanfront village boasting dozens of homes built in the 1700s.  Over lunch, Jennifer recounted a story about an episode of the "Real Housewives" (don't ask) in which one of those snots moaned about having to drive from her house in Southampton "all the way" to Quogue for a party.
        </p>
        <p>
         After lunch, we did that exact drive in reverse, which took maybe 25 minutes.  And as we were walking down the street in Southampton, we overheard a woman at an outdoor cafe complain to her friend, "So, I have to go to this party tonight . . . but it's all the way out in
         <em>
          Quogue
         </em>
         !"  Poor Quogue.  So close, and yet so far away.  I guess that explains why I don't have any photos of it.
        </p>
        <h3>
         R is for Rumba.
        </h3>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Rumba_09.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Rumba_09.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_RumbaRedos_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_RumbaRedos_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_RumbaRedos_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_RumbaRedos_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Rumba_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Rumba_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         We all dream of a place like "Cheers," where we can walk in and everybody knows our name (and, more importantly, what we'd like to drink).  Rumba is our Cheers.  So close that we can bike there (not that we ever do - that would be a little too much like exercise), Rumba's got it all:  A slew of Adirondack chairs at the water's edge, plentiful seating outside on the deck, friendly servers, fantastic food, and the best drinks in the Hamptons, most of which are served "Bigga" style in oversized Mason jars.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Rumba_Sangria_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Rumba_Sangria_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Rumahi_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Rumahi_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Rumbasweet_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Rumbasweet_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Rumba_03.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Rumba_03.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="PricklyPear.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/PricklyPear.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Rumba_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Rumba_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Rumba_02.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Rumba_02.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         In season, Rumba operates a tiki-themed RumBarge that runs back and forth between Rumba and its sister restaurant, Cowfish, and is operated by a guy who I swear is
         <em>
          not
         </em>
         wearing a pirate costume.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Rumba_23.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Rumba_23.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Rumba_19.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Rumba_19.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Rumba_15.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Rumba_15.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Best of all, there's free shots of homemade banana-vanilla rum for the regulars.  And even the irregulars.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_RumbaRum_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_RumbaRum_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         S is for Shelter Island.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Remember Howard Hughes, the fabulously wealthy yet famously reclusive business magnate and aviator who, in order to avoid conflicts with the owners of the penthouse hotel suite he'd been occupying for years, simply bought the hotel so he'd never have to leave?
        </p>
        <p>
         Shelter Island is a lot like that.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="65949A812219AC68178B4693DFA960C9.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/65949A812219AC68178B4693DFA960C9.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_shelteragain_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_shelteragain_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         How else to describe a 9-square mile island just minutes from the chi-chi Hamptons that doesn't have a movie theatre, bookstore, a single traffic light . . . or a bridge to the mainland?
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="659567492219AC68177D5FB1C2007ECC.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/659567492219AC68177D5FB1C2007ECC.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_shelteragain_3.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_shelteragain_3.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         All of which sounds delightful, but for now we're staying  put.
         <a href="http://traceyg.travellerspoint.com/42/">
          Experience has taught us
         </a>
         that relying on a boat to get to lunch or dinner can result in unacceptably long delays while you untangle your anchor line from around the propeller, or whatever.
        </p>
        <h3>
         T is for tomatoes.
        </h3>
        <p>
         As you probably know, I am obsessed with tomatoes.  And so we spend a good part of the summer chasing down the Tomato Lady in Sag Harbor and buying up the multicolored heirlooms at Hayground Market for the one thing I can "cook" that always comes out perfectly: mozzarella and tomato salad with a drizzle of aged balsamic.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Tomatoes_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Tomatoes_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Tomatoes_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Tomatoes_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         And last summer, I gleefully welcomed the debut of the biggest, baddest tomato event of them all: A tasting of 55 of the whopping 350 varieties of heirloom tomatoes grown from seed by tomato goddess Steph Gaylor at Invincible Summer Farms in Southold, including oddballs like the Amazon Chocolate tomato and the Chartruese Mutant.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Tomatoes_3.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Tomatoes_3.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Perhaps not surprisingly, I was the only one who brought my own salt shaker, prompting a photographer from Newsday to follow me around all afternoon.
        </p>
        <p>
         <a class="enlarge_image" href="/image_enlarge.cfm?src=http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_zzz_8.jpg" onclick="raw_popup(this);return false" title="Click for full size image">
          <img alt="2014_zzz_8.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/thumb_2014_zzz_8.jpg"/>
         </a>
        </p>
        <p>
         Now I know how poor Angel feels.
        </p>
        <h3>
         U is for Umbrella Beach.
        </h3>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_13.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_13.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Umbrella_11.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Umbrella_11.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Every Fourth of July, I manage to convince Angel to make the drive out to Montauk for a sunset dinner, followed by the "Stars Over Montauk" fireworks display at Umbrella Beach.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Umbrella_12.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Umbrella_12.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         We usually end up at Gosman's Dock, a quaint shopping and dining district where you can watch the boats come in with the day's catch . . . or watch the fog roll in and destroy all of the carefully-coiffed hair in its path.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Umbrella_15.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Umbrella_15.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_07.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_07.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_09.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_09.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_02.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_02.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_03.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_03.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_08.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_08.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Umbrella_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Umbrella_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Angel has teased me for years about my obsession with fireworks, and the display at Umbrella Beach does not disappoint.  Put on by the famous Grucci family, which handles the over-the-top pyrotechnics for presidential inaugurations and the Olympics, the Stars Over Montauk display runs for nearly an hour, eliciting a series of oohs and aahs from the lucky spectators.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_17.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_17.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Umbrella_16.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Umbrella_16.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <div class="video">
         <iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="281" mozallowfullscreen="" src="http://player.vimeo.com/video/91731590" webkitallowfullscreen="" width="500">
         </iframe>
        </div>
        <p>
         Or maybe that's just me.
        </p>
        <h3>
         V is for vineyards.
        </h3>
        <p>
         With its glacial soil and maritime climate, the east end of Long Island is home to more than 40 wineries, many of which are turning out good-to-very-good Chardonnay and Merlot, along with Sauvignon Blanc, Malbec, Cabernet Franc, and others.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_vineyards_08.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_vineyards_08.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_vineyards_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_vineyards_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         In Napa or Sonoma such small, rustic tasting rooms and family-run operations would be delightful "off-the-beaten-path" finds, but on the North Fork they're business as usual, which suits us just fine.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_vineyards_07.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_vineyards_07.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_vineyards_05.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_vineyards_05.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_vineyards_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_vineyards_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_vineyards_09.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_vineyards_09.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         And down on the South Fork, there's our beloved Channing Daughters in Bridgehampton, also known as the "hippie winery" for its dedication to lesser-known European varietals like Ribolla Gialla, Dornfelder, Blaufrankisch, and Legrein.  I know the end of the previous sentence looks like my fingers landed on the wrong keys, but I assure you they are real words.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_vineyards_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_vineyards_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_AGchan_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_AGchan_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_vineyards_03.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_vineyards_03.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_vineyards_11.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_vineyards_11.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         W is for Wolffer.
        </h3>
        <p>
         I'd still love the Hamptons even if it didn't have wineries, but obviously not as much.  One of our favorites is the stylish Wolffer Estate in Sagaponack.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wolftoobrite_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wolftoobrite_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_08.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_08.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_09.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_09.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         The main winery building is open, airy, and has a small shop where you can buy one of those useless wine-vacuum gadgets.   I mean, who ever has wine
         <em>
          left over
         </em>
         ?
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wolffer_10.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wolffer_10.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_11.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_11.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_18.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_18.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_17.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_17.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Tastings are offered outside on the spacious patio, just a stone's throw from the vines.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_12.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_12.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wolffer_13.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wolffer_13.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_14.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_14.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wolffer_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wolffer_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_03.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_03.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_15.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_15.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         While we love the main winery location for its gorgeous architecture, we actually prefer the winery's smaller offshoot, known as the Wine Stand, which is just a short drive away.  The Wine Stand has a small, uncrowded patio, endless views, and live music on Friday and Saturday evenings for the sunset.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_20.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_20.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_26.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_26.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wolftoobrite_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wolftoobrite_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_21.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_21.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_19.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_19.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         We typically choose the patio for the shade (and proximity to the bar), but the "vineyard" tables are just as lovely.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Wolffer_23.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Wolffer_23.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wolffer_25.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wolffer_25.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Wolffer_24.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Wolffer_24.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Best of all, you can arrive by scooter, or by Rolls Royce.  Your choice, obviously.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_WolfferRolls_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_WolfferRolls_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         X is for x-citing cars.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Okay, that's a stretch, but there are not alot of xylophones or x-rays in the Hamptons, and really, where else can you see so many ridiculously cute, sherbet-colored cars in one place?
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Hamptoncars_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Hamptoncars_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Hamptoncars_5.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Hamptoncars_5.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Hamptoncars_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Hamptoncars_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_yellowcar_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_yellowcar_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_HamptoncarCoral_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_HamptoncarCoral_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_silveragain_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_silveragain_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Hamptoncars_7.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Hamptoncars_7.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Hamptoncars_8.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Hamptoncars_8.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Hamptoncars_3.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Hamptoncars_3.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         Y is for yachts.
        </h3>
        <p>
         While most middle-aged men try to show off their virility with a shiny new sports car, that trick doesn't work in the Hamptons, since even the plumbers are driving Maseratis.  So the next-best, um, yardstick is the mega-yacht.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Yachtss_5.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Yachtss_5.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Yachtss_3.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Yachtss_3.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="doubleyachts.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/doubleyachts.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_Yachtss_9.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_Yachtss_9.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Yachtss_8.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Yachtss_8.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Preferably equipped with a crew in matching polos, a Jeep, and a whole other normal-sized boat.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_yachtcrew.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_yachtcrew.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Yachtss_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Yachtss_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_Yachtss_6.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_Yachtss_6.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         Z is for catching up on our Zzzs.
        </h3>
        <p>
         When you live and work in the city that never sleeps, being well-rested during the week is like being sober on the weekends: It's an admirable goal, but does anyone ever really achieve it?  And so, by the time the weekend rolls around, Angel and I are ready to
         <em>
          loll
         </em>
         around.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_zzz_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_zzz_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_zzz_3.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_zzz_3.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_zzz_4.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_zzz_4.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_zzz_7.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_zzz_7.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_zzz_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_zzz_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_AGNap_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_AGNap_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2014_AGNap_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2014_AGNap_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2014_zzz_6.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2014_zzz_6.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         The Hamptons.  They may be glitzy, glamorous, and sometimes even grating, but there's no better place to get your sloth on.
        </p>
        <p>
         ------------------------------------------

           and you'll be notified when a new post goes up!

        </p>

      <div class="entry">
       <h2 class="entrytitle" id="Entry89">
        <a href="http://traceyg.travellerspoint.com/89/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent link to The BVIs, Part 1: BBQ, Boulders, and Blacklists">
         The BVIs, Part 1: BBQ, Boulders, and Blacklists
        </a>
       </h2>
       <p class="preentrydetails">
        <span class="entrydate">
         01.31.2014
        </span>
       </p>
       <div class="entrycontent">
        <p>
         When
         <a href="http://traceyg.travellerspoint.com/42/">
          your last tropical vacation
         </a>
         involved unimaginable horrors like low water pressure and plastic wine glasses and a boat nicknamed "The Divorcinator," the last thing you want on your next vacation is to rough it.  On your next vacation, you want to be pampered.  You want all of the high-end luxuries you missed on your last trip, like electricity and real silverware and hot water.  And you most definitely want someone
         <em>
          else
         </em>
         to drive the boat.
        </p>
        <p>
         We found all that and more on our recent trip to the British Virgin Islands.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="SpitRedo.gif" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/SpitRedo.gif"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_BoatOpener_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_BoatOpener_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_OpenBeach_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_OpenBeach_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_arrival_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_arrival_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Now, I know that most folks who frequent the BVIs are hardy souls who live aboard their sailboats and take quick Navy showers and don't own hair dryers.  And to them I say, you have my utmost respect.  I, too, have lived as one with nature -- on our last vacation, for example, there was a large spider in our house that made it impossible to get to the ironing board -- and I know that it takes a special kind of person to spend a week or two peeing in what amounts to a bouncing broom closet.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_BoatOpener_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_BoatOpener_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Our ten days of soaking up the
         <span style="text-decoration:line-through;display:inline;">
          modern conveniences
         </span>
         sunshine began after a short direct flight from New York, when we arrived in St. Thomas, hopped the ferry over to Tortola, picked up our 4-wheel-drive, buckled ourselves in, and wedged our overstuffed luggage in place to serve as makeshift airbags.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_05.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_05.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         That's because driving on Tortola is not for the faint of heart, or the fearful of heights, or the lover of life.  Imagine that you're in the front car on a roller coaster.  You approach the first steep incline and the coaster begins its ascent, inching its way up, up, up, until it's almost at the top, and then that dreaded clicking sound slows to a excruciating pace.
         <em>
          Click . . . click . . . . . click . . . . . .
         </em>
         And then comes that final lone
         <em>
          click
         </em>
         , and for one terrifying heartbeat there's complete silence.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_CarTilt_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_CarTilt_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_10.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_10.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         The front car of the coaster peeks hesitantly over the edge of that first drop, and then, with an audible
         <em>
          whoosh
         </em>
         , the car suddenly plummets over the edge at breakneck speed, only to barrel full-tilt up the next incline, repeating the cycle until your eyes are watering, your stomach is flip-flopping, and your white knuckles have to be pried from the safety bar.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_09.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_09.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Now, throw in a dirt track studded with potholes and rocks; switchbacks set at absurdly steep angles; obstacles like goats, chickens, sinkholes, and hitchhikers; and a distracting postcard view around every turn, and you have a good idea of what it's like to drive on Tortola.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_arrival_14.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_arrival_14.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         I realize this might sound daunting, but it's actually not all bad.  For example, unlike on most other Caribbean islands, on Tortola you don't need to worry about remembering to drive on the left.  That's because everyone drives straight down the middle of the road, swerving into their proper lane only at the last possible second, involving you in an unwitting game of chicken every time you leave the house.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_yellowhouse_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_yellowhouse_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         And so it was with some trepidation that we double-checked our seat belts and followed the property manager up a one-lane burro path of rocks and rut and dizzying precipices to the house we'd rented for our stay, the charming Peach Cottage, which rewarded us with breathtaking views of St. John and the islands beyond.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_11.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_11.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_17.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_17.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_PoolDay_11.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_PoolDay_11.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_HouseBriter_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_HouseBriter_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_19.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_19.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_PoolDay_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_PoolDay_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_PoolDay_05.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_PoolDay_05.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_20.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_20.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_PoolDay_07.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_PoolDay_07.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_arrival_21.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_arrival_21.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         The house also came with a sweet little cat named Bella.  We quickly developed a mutually beneficial relationship, like those tiny birds that eat the bugs off hippos: I rubbed her belly and scratched her ears, and she kept the scarier tropical creatures that would have otherwise invaded our house at bay.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Bella_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Bella_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Bella_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Bella_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         After getting acquainted with the house, we ran the route from the main road to the house one more time in the waning daylight to make sure we'd be able to find our way back at night -- left at the superette with the stray dogs outside; right at the crumbling yellow retaining wall; left at the house with the cow tied up in the front yard -- and then settled in to watch the sunset.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_arrival_30.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_arrival_30.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_PCSunset_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_PCSunset_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_PCSunset_5.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_PCSunset_5.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Soon we were hungry, and it was time to head out for some dinner.  We'd driven on Tortola before, but our skills were rusty, so what better way to sharpen them up than with a first-night drive up and over the mountain . . . in the rain?  Sure, that sounds stupid, but when Myett's BBQ ribs are at stake, you'd duct-tape yourself to a blind, three-legged mule to get there.
        </p>
        <p>
         Angel has been teasing me for years about our last visit to Myett's, where I'd ordered the chicken because I liked the sound of their spiced-rum-and-tamarind BBQ sauce.  Now, I am not a big fan of chicken.  Not because it's dry (which it is), or because it's boring (which it is), but because it is often full of unpleasant surprises.  Nobody ever finds a random vein or tendon in a bowl of spaghetti, but in a chicken breast?  It's like a gristle-y pinata.
        </p>
        <p>
         But that BBQ sauce at Myett's sounded so good that I ordered the chicken.  A
         <em>
          half
         </em>
         -chicken, replete with bones and tendons and veins and those rubbery joint-socket things and god knows what else.
        </p>
        <p>
         But oh, that sauce was good.  It was so good that, like a crazed piranha, I proceeded to pick that poor little half-carcass completely clean, as Angel looked on in stunned silence.  I'd never done anything remotely like that before, and I've certainly never picked a chicken clean since, all of which is a very long-winded way of explaining that Myett's serves some damn fine BBQ sauce.
        </p>
        <p>
         And so we piled into the car and headed off to Cane Garden Bay.  All was going fine until the we reached the last switchback, a hairpin turn set on an angle so steep that it's impossible to see the oncoming traffic, even at night.  The only way to take the curve is by going wide, into the oncoming lane.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_15.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_15.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Me, I'd have closed my eyes and crossed my fingers and taken the turn wide.  But Angel is a rule-follower.  He always does the right thing, even when the right thing means almost certain death.  And so he stayed in his own lane.  But the angle of the switchback was just too steep; the turning radius too narrow.  The car began to lose its grip on the road, and we began to slide back down the mountain . . . on our backs . . . in the rain . . . without a guard rail.
        </p>
        <p>
         Even roller coasters don't usually do
         <em>
          that
         </em>
         .
        </p>
        <p>
         Eventually we made it to Myett's, where we devoured tamarind ribs and coconut polenta and nerve-calming cocktails, and Angel inquired about a long-term rental so he wouldn't have to drive back up and over the mountain.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_arrival_29.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_arrival_29.jpg"/>
         <br/>
         <br/>
         Of course we did make it back, and were greeted at the house by creatures great and small.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_lizard_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_lizard_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_26.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_26.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Very small.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_arrival_25.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_arrival_25.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Obviously I'm getting the short end of the stick in this deal with the cat.
        </p>
        <p>
         The next day we awoke to a glorious view.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Morning_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Morning_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         And if we hadn't already planned a day trip to Virgin Gorda, we'd probably still be lazing around in that bed.  But one of the things we like best about the BVIs is its generally efficient ferry system (even if most of the schedules do require you to get out of bed before noon).  Some of the ferries are less, um, sea-worthy-looking than others, but for the most part they are fast, on-time, and inexpensive.  Best of all, the ferry boats are typically operated by people who know how to drive them and dock them and avoid grounding them, which was a nice change for us.  Ahem.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_VGferry_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_VGferry_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_VGferry_2.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_VGferry_2.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Upon arrival in Virgin Gorda we picked up the car we'd rented for the day, which came with an air freshener that probably doesn't sell too well north of the Mason-Dixon line.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_74.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_74.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         It also came with a set of keys, which Angel proceeded to confuse with our other set of keys . . . for our rental vehicle back on Tortola.  Now, I understand that normal people do stuff like this all the time.  But in the nearly 20 years that I have known Angel, he has never so much as forgotten his keys, or temporarily misplaced them, or lost a pair of gloves, or left an umbrella behind at a restaurant.  Do you know what it's like to live with someone who has never experienced a Senior Moment,
         <em>
          ever
         </em>
         ???
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         It is maddening.
        </p>
        <p>
         Thus it is with no small amount of glee that I tell you that Angel spent a good 15 minutes trying the (wrong) keys over and over and wondering how he'd locked himself out of a car that had been working fine when we picked it up just five minutes earlier.  Eventually he gave up and used the phone at the Top of the Baths to call the rental company and inform them about the "faulty" keys; later, of course, he had to call them again once he figured out his mistake.
        </p>
        <p>
         I am not ashamed to admit that watching him make that phone call was the highlight of this vacation, if not this year.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_07.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_07.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Once my 15 minutes of glory were up, our first stop was to re-visit the Baths.  We hadn't been there in about six years, and back then Angel had to convince me that checking out a bunch of boulders was a worthwhile way to spend a day.  I had been decidedly unimpressed by the time we reached the end of the path, not realizing that we hadn't even started yet, and that the "cave" is where the Baths really begin.
        </p>
        <p>
         <a class="enlarge_image" href="/image_enlarge.cfm?src=http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_CaveSign_1.jpg" onclick="raw_popup(this);return false" title="Click for full size image">
          <img alt="2013_BVI_CaveSign_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/thumb_2013_BVI_CaveSign_1.jpg"/>
         </a>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_08.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_08.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_03.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_03.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         And so we slipped on our water shoes (the Baths are no place for any footwear that is not water-friendly and preferably equipped with suction cups on the soles) and took that same route this time around, following the narrow path down to the beach and the entrance to the cave.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_16.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_16.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_14.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_14.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_15.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_15.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_17.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_17.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_19.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_19.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_20.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_20.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_18.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_18.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_21.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_21.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_22.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_22.jpg"/>
         <br/>
         <br/>
         The last time we were here, we didn't know much about the Baths, so we'd asked our elderly taxi driver, and his equally ancient buddy who'd come along for the ride, exactly how the boulders at the Baths had ended up there, expecting to hear something about volcanoes or landslides or shifting tectonic plates.  Instead, both men had looked at each other, then replied with the exact same answer, at the exact same moment: "
         <em>
          Creation
         </em>
         ."  And the truth is, whether you believe in a higher power or not, it's easy to believe that the island's volcanic origins only partly explain how these massive granite boulders came to be strewn on the beach and balanced precariously on top of one another, as if tossed by the hand of a giant.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_45.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_45.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_52.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_52.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_63.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_63.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_26.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_26.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_64.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_64.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         We spent the next two hours picking our way among the boulders, squeezing and shimmying and sliding our way along, all the while marveling at their immense size and ethereal beauty.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_24.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_24.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_27.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_27.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Strips_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Strips_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_28.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_28.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_30.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_30.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_31.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_31.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_37.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_37.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_38.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_38.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Occasionally it wasn't clear which way we should go, but there were a few hints.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_32.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_32.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_40.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_40.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_39.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_39.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_41.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_41.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_42.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_42.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_46.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_46.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_47.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_47.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_34.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_34.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_35.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_35.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Before our visit, I'd seen a review online which said that the Baths were no place for anyone over 40, which cracked me up.  Then I climbed these 85 flights of stairs and cursed my own hubris.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_50.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_50.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_51.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_51.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_53.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_53.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_48.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_48.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_49.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_49.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_54.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_54.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_55.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_55.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_60.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_60.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_62.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_62.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         The path ends at the beach, which on this overcast day lent an eerie grey tinge to the mossy, water-worn boulders.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_57.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_57.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_58.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_58.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_59.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_59.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         After a short rest and a quick swim, it was time to head back.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_66.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_66.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_BathBeach_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_BathBeach_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_69.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_69.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_BathView_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_BathView_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_71.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_71.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_72.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_72.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_70.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_70.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Afterwards, we rewarded ourselves for not tearing our ACLs in the face of nearly insurmountable odds with a couple of frozen drinks at Top of the Baths.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_Baths_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_Baths_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_Baths_10.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_Baths_10.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_BathDrinks_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_BathDrinks_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Indeed, we were enjoying ourselves so much that it wasn't until 11:37 that I suddenly remembered that I'd made reservations for lunch at Little Dix Bay . . . at 11:30.  This couldn't be happening!  It was like one of those dreams where you show up for your final exam 3 hours late.  You see, I am a planner with a capital P.  I am organized and on time.  I never miss an appointment (and never,
         <em>
          ever
         </em>
         miss a meal), and if I'm going to be late, I call.  Things don't just slip my mind.  And yet, the reservation at Little Dix had done just that, leaving me embarrassed and wondering if forgetting a lunch reservation is the first step toward forgetting that your pants should stop at your waist, not your ribcage, and that sandals should be worn
         <em>
          sans
         </em>
         socks.
        </p>
        <p>
         And so I urged Angel to leadfoot it over to Little Dix, while he reminded me that we were on island time, and reassured me that they probably wouldn't notice if we were an entire hour late, let alone 10 minutes.  He's probably right, I told myself.  Heck, they probably never even put me in the reservation book . . . if they even have one, that is.  We made a quick pit stop for directions to avoid the possibility of misreading our map, and were instructed to turn "at the gap," which (we eventually determined) refers not to the place where you buy khakis but to the place where you can next make a right or left turn.
        </p>
        <p>
         Luckily the resort wasn't far, and in short order we found ourselves at the Little Dix security gate.  We explained that we were here for lunch.  And then the security guard uttered the most humiliating words I have ever heard.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixGen_13.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixGen_13.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         "Oh," she said, eyeing a Log of Latecomers apparently inscribed with my name, social security number, and date of birth.  "You're the 11:30 people."
        </p>
        <p>
         "You're the 11:30 people"?!?  I was mortified.  I slunk down in my seat so she couldn't get a good look at me and mumbled something about island time and the Gap.  She radioed ahead to the restaurant and repeated the damning words -- "The 11:30 people are here!" -- motioning us through the gate and making some kind of notation in the Log that I am sure will follow me around for the rest of my life, like a blacklist for lollygaggers.
        </p>
        <p>
         We parked the car, raced down the winding path, and arrived sweaty and panting . . .
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixGen_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixGen_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="large_2013_BVI_DixGen_10.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/large_2013_BVI_DixGen_10.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         . . . to a completely empty restaurant.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_01.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_01.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         That's right:  They were expecting the 11:30 people . . . because we were the
         <em>
          only
         </em>
         people.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_04.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_04.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         By this time I was so stressed out that despite the Beach Grill's lovely menu of grilled fish and salads and other island fare, I went straight for the pepperoni pizza.  Nothing says "It's okay to be 12 minutes late" like extra cheese.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_14.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_14.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Once you make the decision to eat an entire pepperoni pizza for lunch, you might as well have a bowl of homemade potato chips and a Bailey's banana colada, too.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_11.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_11.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_07.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_07.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_06.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_06.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixTTG2_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixTTG2_1.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         We also had a Planter's punch, a bowl of gazpacho, the grilled fish, and some of the best tuna tartare I have ever had.  Which didn't work out too well for Angel, since he's the one who ordered it.
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_12.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_12.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_15.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_15.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_05.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_05.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="2013_BVI_DixLunch_13.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_DixLunch_13.jpg"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         At least I think he was.  You know what they say: Once you hit 40, no more climbing ladders for you, or remembering who ate what for lunch.
        </p>
        <p>
         If you can even remember to show up, that is.
         <br/>
         ------------------------------------------------------------------------
         <br/>
         <strong>
          The next day was Christmas, and it was the worst one since that year I received a pink bottle labeled "toilet water" and realized that Santa really
          <em>
           was
          </em>
          keeping a list.
          <a href="http://traceyg.travellerspoint.com/90/  ">
           Click here
          </a>
          for Part 2, or
          <a href="http://traceyg.travellerspoint.com/subscribe/">
           click here to subscribe
          </a>
          and you'll be the first to know when a new post goes up!
         </strong>
        </p>
        <p>
         <a class="enlarge_image" href="/image_enlarge.cfm?src=http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/2013_BVI_catredo_1.jpg" onclick="raw_popup(this);return false" title="Click for full size image">
          <img alt="2013_BVI_catredo_1.jpg" class="photo" src="http://photos.travellerspoint.com/293321/thumb_2013_BVI_catredo_1.jpg"/>
         </a>
        </p>
       </div>
